###begin article-title 0
###xml 47 48 43 44 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 108 109 104 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn1">*</xref>
###xml 109 111 105 107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn3">S&#8414;</xref>
Rac Regulates Its Effector Phospholipase Cgamma2 through Interaction with a Split Pleckstrin Homology Domain*Sâƒž
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1

###end p 1

###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>
Author's Choice
###end p 3
###begin p 4
 applies to Author Choice Articles
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 201 202 193 194 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 358 359 346 347 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 627 628 607 608 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 694 695 670 671 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1057 1058 1029 1030 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1071 1072 1039 1040 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
Several isoforms of phospholipase C (PLC) are regulated through interactions with Ras superfamily GTPases, including Rac proteins. Interestingly, of two closely related PLCgamma isoforms, only PLCgamma2 has previously been shown to be activated by Rac. Here, we explore the molecular basis of this interaction as well as the structural properties of PLCgamma2 required for activation. Based on reconstitution experiments with isolated PLCgamma variants and Rac2, we show that an unusual pleckstrin homology (PH) domain, designated as the split PH domain (spPH), is both necessary and sufficient to effect activation of PLCgamma2 by Rac2. We also demonstrate that Rac2 directly binds to PLCgamma2 as well as to the isolated spPH of this isoform. Furthermore, through the use of NMR spectroscopy and mutational analysis, we determine the structure of spPH, define the structural features of spPH required for Rac interaction, and identify critical amino acid residues at the interaction interface. We further discuss parallels and differences between PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 and the implications of our findings for their respective signaling roles.
###end p 5

###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 47 48 47 48 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn5">3</xref>
###xml 451 452 429 430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref1">1</xref>
###xml 453 454 431 432 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref3">3</xref>
###xml 506 507 476 477 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 520 521 486 487 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 845 846 811 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 921 925 887 891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g.</italic>
###xml 1293 1294 1255 1256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 1296 1297 1258 1259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
Phosphoinositide-specific phospholipase C (PLC)3 enzymes have been established as crucial signaling nodes involved in regulation of a variety of cellular functions via hydrolysis of the membrane lipid phosphatidylinositol 4,5-bisphosphate. There are six major families of PLC enzymes (PLCbeta,-gamma,-delta,-epsilon,-zeta, and -eta) that share a common core of domains related to catalysis and are distinguished by family-specific regulatory regions (1-3). The two isoforms of the PLCgamma family, PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2, uniquely incorporate an array of domains comprising two SH2 domains, an SH3 domain, and an internal or "split" PH domain (spPH). spPHs represent a unique subclass of PH domains that are characterized by insertions of one or several autonomously folded protein modules encoded within the boundaries of PH domain sequences (4). This array also contains sites for phosphorylation by several receptor (e.g. epidermal growth factor and platelet-derived growth factor receptors) and nonreceptor tyrosine kinases. In addition to tyrosine phosphorylation, multiple protein-protein interactions (mainly mediated by SH2 and SH3 domains) contribute to PLCgamma activation and have an important role in localizing the enzyme to protein complexes in different cellular compartments (5, 6). However, the elucidation at the molecular level of how PLCgamma isoforms are regulated remains an area of intense study.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 61 62 57 58 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 75 76 67 68 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 182 183 174 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref7">7</xref>
###xml 185 186 177 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 220 221 208 209 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 276 277 260 261 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 448 449 428 429 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 548 552 528 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g.</italic>
###xml 783 784 759 760 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 797 798 769 770 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 800 801 772 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref9">9</xref>
###xml 802 804 774 776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref11">11</xref>
###xml 888 889 856 857 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 902 903 866 867 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1008 1010 968 970 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref11">11</xref>
###xml 1097 1098 1049 1050 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1147 1149 1099 1101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
Despite the common domain organization shared by the PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 isoforms, studies using gene-targeting approaches demonstrated that each has a distinct biological role (7, 8). Different functions of PLCgamma1 (essential role in embryonic development) and PLCgamma2 (requirement for development and function of hematopoietic cells) to some degree reflect their different expression patterns and, in particular, the abundance of PLCgamma2 in hematopoietic cells. However, studies of different cell types where both isoforms are present (e.g. platelets, macrophages/monocytes, granulocytes, and NK cells) have shown that one isoform can be preferentially activated over the other, suggesting that additional mechanisms must exist to determine the distinct roles of PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 (9-11). Overall, studies of proteins that bind to SH2 and SH3 domains and target PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 to signaling complexes suggest that these binding partners are not specific to either PLCgamma isoform (11). However, a recent analysis of the two PLCgamma isoforms has shown that only PLCgamma2 can be activated by the Rho family GTPase, Rac (12). Importantly, this was the first report to identify a signaling component that could provide a basis for differential regulation of these two closely related PLCgamma isoforms.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 36 37 32 33 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 460 462 452 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref13">13</xref>
###xml 464 466 456 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref14">14</xref>
###xml 556 557 545 546 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 567 569 556 558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 571 573 560 562 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 688 690 671 673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 691 693 674 676 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref20">20</xref>
###xml 721 722 700 701 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 812 814 791 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
###xml 1207 1209 1180 1182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref22">22</xref>
###xml 1308 1309 1278 1279 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1329 1331 1299 1301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
###xml 1500 1501 1467 1468 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1514 1516 1481 1483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref24">24</xref>
###xml 1517 1519 1484 1486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref26">26</xref>
###xml 1760 1762 1727 1729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref27">27</xref>
The report of activation of PLCgamma2 by Rac has also expanded the scope of potential regulators of the PLCgamma family and is in line with the interconnection between other Ras superfamily GTPases and PLC isoforms. Thus, although the possible role of small GTPases in the activation of phosphoinositide-specific PLC was noted over 20 years ago, it is only recently that progress has been made in uncovering the identity of the interacting protein components (13, 14). Initially, it was reported that Rac GTPases and Cdc42 specifically activate the PLCbeta2 isoform (15, 16). The recently discovered PLCepsilon isoform was reported to be regulated by specific Ras and Rho family GTPases (17-20). In addition, the PLCdelta1 isoform has been implicated in binding to Ral GTPases, leading to subsequent activation (21). Furthermore, recent studies have defined the structural basis for select examples of these interactions. For example, the crystal structure of activated H-Ras bound to the isolated PLCepsilon RA2 domain revealed an interaction surface that is distinctly different from those of other known Ras effectors (c-Raf, RalGDS, and phosphatidylinositol 3-kinase) that contain the same RA/RBD fold (22). More recently, the crystal structure of activated Rac1 bound to a C-terminally truncated PLCbeta2 has been reported (23), in which the interaction interface is restricted to the N-terminal PH domain, a region previously implicated as a key structural determinant for Rac-dependent PLCbeta2 activation (24-26). This Rac-PH domain complex has expanded the structural diversity of domain types involved in binding Rho family GTPases and highlighted the potential role of PH domains as a site for either protein-lipid and protein-protein interactions (27).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 100 101 96 97 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 115 116 107 108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 161 162 149 150 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 199 200 184 185 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 257 258 238 239 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 336 337 314 315 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 403 404 377 378 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 544 545 514 515 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 558 559 524 525 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
Here, we report an investigation of the structural basis of the Rac binding specificity for PLCgamma2 over PLCgamma1 and how Rac-dependent activation of PLCgamma2 compares with that found for PLCbeta2. We uncover a specific mode of interaction with PLCgamma2 that involves the spPH rather than the N-terminal PH domain common to PLCbeta2. Determination of the three-dimensional structure of the PLCgamma2 spPH and identification of residues critical for Rac binding further identify relatively subtle differences between highly similar PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 isoforms, resulting in distinct selectivity for Rac regulatory proteins, important for their function in cellular signaling.
###end p 14
###begin title 15
EXPERIMENTAL PROCEDURES
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 0 23 0 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Construction of Vectors</italic>
###xml 54 57 54 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myc</italic>
###xml 87 88 83 84 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 144 145 136 137 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 319 324 311 316 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(L/S)</underline>
###xml 374 375 362 363 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 388 389 372 373 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 73 78 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 130 135 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Construction of Vectors-Complementary DNAs encoding c-myc epitope-tagged human PLCgamma1 (1291 aa, accession number ABB84466) and human PLCgamma2 (1265 aa, accession number NP_002652) were inserted into pcDNA3.1(-) and pVL1393 or pcDNA3.1(+) and pVL1392, respectively. The epitope was attached to the carboxyl termini ((L/S)EQKLISEEDL, carboxyl-terminal residues of PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2 underlined).
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 54 55 50 51 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 68 69 60 61 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 374 375 350 351 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 423 424 395 396 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 470 471 438 439 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 521 522 485 486 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 530 531 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 524 531 488 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 589 592 553 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myc</italic>
###xml 747 748 695 696 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 771 772 715 716 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 832 833 772 773 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 845 846 781 782 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 932 935 868 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myc</italic>
###xml 1024 1026 953 955 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref28">28</xref>
###xml 1100 1101 1026 1027 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1142 1143 1064 1065 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1225 1228 1147 1150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myc</italic>
###xml 1459 1460 1349 1350 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1496 1497 1382 1383 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1615 1617 1501 1503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref29">29</xref>
###xml 1893 1902 1775 1784 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">YPYDVPDYA</underline>
###xml 1905 1906 1787 1788 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M</italic>
###xml 1948 1951 1830 1833 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">189</sup>
###xml 1087 1092 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1750 1755 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
In our discussion of the chimeric versions of PLCgamma1 and PLCgamma2, the following nomenclature will be used: PLCgammaW-XYZ, where W refers to the PLCgamma isoform backbone; X, the amino-terminal PH domain; Y, the N-terminal portion of spPH; and Z, the C-terminal portion of spPH. According to this designation, for example, construct PLCgamma1-122 corresponds to PLCgamma1 with the amino-terminal PH domain from PLCgamma1, the N-terminal portion of spPH from PLCgamma2, and the C-terminal portion of spPH from PLCgamma2 (Fig. 1A). For construction of the cDNAs encoding the chimeric, c-myc epitope-tagged PLCgamma enzymes PLCgamma1-211 and PLCgamma2-122, two separate cDNA fragments, one encoding the amino-terminal PH domain of either PLCgamma1 (aa 1-144) or PLCgamma2 (aa 1-133) and the other encoding the remainder of PLCgamma2 or PLCgamma1 followed by the epitope tag, were obtained by PCR and joined together. The cDNA of c-myc epitope-tagged PLCgamma1-beta11 was constructed using the PCR overlap extension method (28) to join the cDNAs encoding the amino-terminal PH domain of human PLCbeta2 (aa 1-137) to the cDNA encoding PLCgamma1 without its amino-terminal PH domain (aa 145-1291). The cDNAs of the chimeric, c-myc epitope-tagged PLCgamma isozymes PLCgamma1-112, PLCgamma1-121, PLCgamma1-122, PLCgamma2-212, PLCgamma2-221, and PLCgamma2-211, in which one or both portions of the split PH domain of one isozyme (aa 482-527 and 872-937 of PLCgamma1; aa 468-513 and 849-914 of PLCgamma2) were replaced by the corresponding regions of the other, were constructed using a two-step megaprimer PCR protocol (29). The primer sequences and PCR protocols are available from the authors upon request. The cDNA of a deletion mutant (Delta1-188) of human Vav1 was amplified by PCR and ligated into pcDNA3.1(+) already containing a DNA sequence encoding the 12CA5 hemagglutinin epitope tag (MGYPYDVPDYAGGSM; hemagglutinin epitope underlined and Met189 of Vav1 shown in italic type).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 175 191 175 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 201 202 197 198 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 243 244 231 232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 333 337 317 321 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G12V</sup>
###xml 63 68 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 175 191 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
To prepare a baculovirus encoding GST-tagged Rac2, the cDNA of human Rac2 was inserted into the baculovirus transfer vector pAc2GT (Pharmingen). For expression of proteins in Escherichia coli (PLCgamma1 spPH, aa 485-936, Delta530-864; PLCgamma2 spPH, aa 471-913, Delta516-841, wild type, and mutants K862I, V893Q, and F897Q; and Rac2G12V, aa 2-177), the particular cDNAs were cloned into the pTriEx4 vector (Novagen) using the Ek/LIC methodology following the manufacturer's instructions. All expression constructs were PCR-amplified with a TeV protease recognition sequence followed by a GGSGGS linker followed by the domain open reading frame.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 0 39 0 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Expression and Purification of Proteins</italic>
###xml 510 511 498 499 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">9</sup>
###xml 761 762 743 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 818 819 800 801 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 822 823 804 805 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 826 827 808 809 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 834 835 816 817 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 838 839 820 821 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 841 842 823 824 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 849 850 831 832 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 862 863 844 845 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 883 884 865 866 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">9</sup>
###xml 1017 1018 999 1000 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">9</sup>
###xml 1068 1069 1050 1051 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1091 1092 1073 1074 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1102 1103 1084 1085 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1125 1126 1107 1108 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1139 1140 1121 1122 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1145 1146 1127 1128 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1153 1154 1135 1136 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1234 1235 1213 1214 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1371 1372 1350 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 1496 1497 1469 1470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 1597 1598 1564 1565 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">9</sup>
###xml 1686 1687 1653 1654 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1876 1877 1837 1838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 1974 1975 1929 1930 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 235 239 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">calf</span>
Expression and Purification of Proteins-For production of recombinant isoprenylated Rac2, baculovirus-infected insect (Sf9) cells (Invitrogen) were grown at 27 degreesC in suspension culture in TNM-FH medium containing 10% (v/v) fetal calf serum (catalog number P04-83500; PAN Biotech, Aidenbach, Germany) supplemented with 0.2% (w/v) Pluronic(R) F-68 (Invitrogen), 50 mug/ml gentamicin (PAA Laboratories), and 2.5 mug/ml amphotericin B (Fungizone(R); Invitrogen) in a 1800-ml Fernbach culture flask. Cells (109 cells/flask) were incubated at 27 degreesC with recombinant baculovirus in 400 ml of medium at 80 rpm on a rotary shaker with an amplitude of 25 mm. Three days after infection, the cells were harvested at room temperature by centrifugation at 300 x g for 5 min and washed once with 100 ml of buffer A (10 mm Na2HPO4, 1.8 mm KH2PO4, 140 mm NaCl, 2.7 mm KCl, pH 7.4) per 109 intact cells at the time of cell harvesting. To obtain detergent-solubilized Rho GTPases, the cells were resuspended in 15 ml per 109 intact cells of ice-cold buffer B containing 20 mm Tris/HCl, pH 8.0, 1 mm EDTA, 1 mm dithiothreitol, 100 mm NaCl, 3.75 mm MgCl2, 0.1 mm phenylmethylsulfonyl fluoride, 1 mug/ml leupeptin, 1 mug/ml aprotinin, and 3 mum GDP and homogenized using a precooled 5-ml Teflon-glass homogenizer. Nuclei and unbroken cells were removed by centrifugation at 300 x g for 10 min at 4 degreesC. The membrane fraction was collected from the resulting supernatant by centrifugation at 12,000 x g for 15 min at 4 degreesC. Rho GTPases were solubilized by resuspending the membranes in 2 ml per 109 intact cells at the time of cell harvesting of ice-cold buffer B supplemented with 23 mm sodium cholate and incubating this mixture for 90 min at 4 degreesC with vigorous vortexing every 10 min. Insoluble material was removed from this suspension by centrifugation at 12,000 x g for 15 min at 4 degreesC. The resulting detergent extract was aliquoted, snap-frozen in liquid N2, and stored at -80 degreesC.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 113 114 103 104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sup>
###xml 284 285 273 274 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">6</sup>
###xml 499 500 482 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 667 668 649 650 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 690 691 672 673 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 737 738 718 719 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 757 758 738 739 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 794 795 774 775 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 811 812 790 791 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1019 1020 997 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 1112 1113 1084 1085 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 203 207 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">calf</span>
###xml 707 714 <span type="species:ncbi:3847">soybean</span>
For production of recombinant PLCgamma isozymes, Sf9 cells were grown at 27 degreesC in adherent culture in 75-cm2 flasks in TNM-FH medium (catalog number T3285; Sigma) supplemented with 10% (v/v) fetal calf serum (catalog number F7524; Sigma) and 50 mug/ml gentamicin. Cells (20 x 106 cells/flask) were incubated with recombinant baculovirus at 27 degreesC in 10 ml of medium/flask. Three days after infection, the cells were detached from the plastic surface, harvested by centrifugation at 300 x g for 5 min at room temperature, washed once at room temperature with 1 ml/flask of buffer A, and then resuspended in 100 mul/flask of ice-cold buffer C containing 20 mm Tris/HCl, pH 7.5, 2 mm EDTA, 2 mug/ml soybean trypsin inhibitor, 3 mm benzamidine, 0.1 mm phenylmethylsulfonyl fluoride, 1 mum pepstatin, 1 mum leupeptin, and 1 mug/ml aprotinin. The cells were homogenized by forcing the suspension ten times through a 0.45 x 25-mm needle attached to a disposable syringe. The homogenate was centrifuged at 100,000 x g for 1 h at 4 degreesC, and the resulting supernatant was aliquoted, snap-frozen in liquid N2, and stored at -80 degreesC.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 2 5 2 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myc</italic>
###xml 281 282 257 258 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 296 298 268 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref30">30</xref>
###xml 398 399 370 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S</italic>
###xml 543 545 515 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 808 809 771 772 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 832 833 795 796 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 843 844 806 807 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 849 850 812 813 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 855 856 818 819 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 953 954 916 917 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
c-myc epitope-tagged PLCgamma1-111, PLCgamma2-222, and PLCgamma1-122 were purified from soluble fractions of baculovirus-infected insect cells grown in suspension culture by sequential chromatography on HiTraptrade mark Heparin HP and MonoQ (GE Healthcare) as described for PLCbeta2Delta in Ref. 30. For purification of posttranslationally modified Rac2, the protein was expressed as a glutathione S-transferase fusion protein in baculovirus-infected insect cells and solubilized from the particulate fraction as described for wild-type Rac2 (12). The protein was purified from the detergent extract by batch adsorption to glutathione-Sepharosetrade mark 4B (GE Healthcare); cleavage of the Rac2 portion from the resin by proteolysis with thrombin (22.5 units/ml 75% (v/v) slurry) in buffer D containing 50 mm Tris/HCl, pH 7.5, 50 mm NaCl, 2 mm MgCl2, 1 mm dithiothreitol, and 0.1% (v/v) Triton X-100; and removal of the protease by batch adsorption to p-aminobenzamidine-agarose (Sigma).
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 30 37 30 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. coli</italic>
###xml 76 78 76 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref31">31</xref>
###xml 83 85 83 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref32">32</xref>
###xml 147 154 147 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. coli</italic>
###xml 205 206 198 199 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 229 230 219 220 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sc>
###xml 315 316 305 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 316 319 306 309 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">600</sub>
###xml 407 409 397 399 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 505 506 495 496 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 521 522 511 512 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 533 534 523 524 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 553 554 543 544 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 634 635 624 625 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 650 651 640 641 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 663 664 653 654 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 683 684 673 674 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 861 862 851 852 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 877 878 867 868 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 888 889 878 879 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1010 1012 994 996 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1377 1378 1361 1362 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1489 1491 1467 1469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref33">33</xref>
###xml 30 37 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 147 154 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Purification of proteins from E. coli was essentially as described in Refs. 31 and 32. Recombinant proteins were expressed from pTriEx4 vectors in E. coli overnight at 25 degreesC in the presence of 100 mum isopropyl 1-thio-beta-d-galactopyranoside (induction was carried out when the bacterial culture attained an A600 of between 0.4 and 1.0). A four-step purification procedure was then adopted. First, Ni2+-chelating chromatography utilizing 5-ml HisTrap columns (GE Healthcare) and wash buffer E (25 mm Tris/Cl, 500 mm NaCl, 40 mm imidazole, and 1 mm tris(2-carboxyethyl)phosphine hydrochloride, pH 8.0) and eluting buffer F (25 mm Tris/Cl, 500 mm NaCl, 500 mm imidazole, and 1 mm tris(2-carboxyethyl) phosphine hydrochloride, pH 8.0). Second, the His and S-tags were proteolytically cleaved overnight by TeV protease in cleavage and dialysis Buffer G (25 mm Tris/Cl, 150 mm NaCl, 1 mm tris(2-carboxyethyl) phosphine hydrochloride, pH 8.0) at 4 degreesC. Third, the cleaved protein mix was passed over a Ni2+-loaded 5-ml HiTrap chelating column (GE Healthcare) in Buffer G, and the flow-through was collected. Last, the flow-through fractions were loaded on a Superdex 75 26/60 gel filtration column (GE Healthcare) in Buffer G, and fractions of monomeric protein were collected and concentrated. Proteins were either used immediately or stored by snap freezing in liquid N2 and transfer to -80 degreesC. Labeled proteins for NMR studies were expressed essentially as outlined in Ref. 33 and purified as described above.
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 0 36 0 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Measurement of PLC Activity in Vitro</italic>
###xml 91 93 91 93 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref30">30</xref>
###xml 95 97 95 97 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>
###xml 273 274 268 269 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 301 302 296 297 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 313 314 308 309 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 326 327 321 322 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 452 453 440 441 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 480 481 468 469 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 490 491 478 479 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 501 502 489 490 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 525 526 512 513 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 560 561 546 547 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 563 564 549 550 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sup>
###xml 712 714 698 700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 888 889 866 867 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1061 1062 1038 1039 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1135 1136 1112 1113 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1227 1228 1204 1205 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1276 1278 1253 1255 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1474 1476 1451 1453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref30">30</xref>
###xml 352 358 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 633 639 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Measurement of PLC Activity in Vitro-Phospholipase C activity was determined as described (30, 34) with minor modifications. In brief, aliquots (10 mul) of the soluble fraction of PLCgamma-baculovirus-infected insect cells appropriately diluted in buffer H, containing 60 mm Tris/maleate, pH 7.3, 84 mm KCl, 3.6 mm EGTA, 2.4 mm dithiothreitol, 2 mg/ml bovine serum albumin, were incubated for 45 min at 30 degreesC in a volume of 60 mul containing 50 mm Tris/maleate, pH 7.3, 70 mm KCl, 3 mm EGTA, 2 mm dithiothreitol, 536 mum phosphatidylethanolamine, 33.4 mum [3H]phosphatidylinositol (4,5)-bisphosphate (185 GBq/mmol), 0.33 mg/ml bovine serum albumin, and the concentrations of sodium deoxycholate and free Ca2+ specified in the figure legends. For reconstitution of wild-type and mutant PLCgamma isozymes with Rac2, the diluted soluble fraction containing the PLC or purified PLCgamma2 was reconstituted with 5 mul of detergent extract containing crude or purified isoprenylated Rac2 and incubated with the phospholipid substrate as described above. Fifty mm HEPES/NaOH, pH 7.2, was present in the incubation medium instead of 50 mm Tris/maleate, pH 7.3, when purified proteins were reconstituted. The concentration of CaCl2 required to adjust the concentration of free Ca2+ to the desired value was calculated using the program EqCal for Windows (Biosoft, Ferguson, MO). The reaction was terminated, and the samples were analyzed for inositol phosphates, as described (30).
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 0 29 0 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cell Culture and Transfection</italic>
###xml 121 122 115 116 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 288 289 282 283 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 486 487 479 480 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">5</sup>
###xml 1028 1029 993 994 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 234 238 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">calf</span>
Cell Culture and Transfection-COS-7 cells were maintained at 37 degreesC in a humidified atmosphere of 90% air and 10% CO2 in Dulbecco's modified Eagle's medium (catalog number 41965-039; Invitrogen) supplemented with 10% (v/v) fetal calf serum (catalog number 10270-106; Invitrogen), 2 mm glutamine, 100 units/ml penicillin, and 100 mug/ml streptomycin (all from PAA Laboratories, Colbe, Germany). Prior to transfection, the cells were seeded into 12-well plates at densities of 1 x 105 cells/well, respectively, and grown for 24 h in 1 ml/well of the same medium. One hour before transfection, the medium was replaced with 1 ml/well of fresh medium. For transfection of COS-7 cells, plasmid DNA (1.0 mug DNA/well) was mixed with 2.0 mul Lipofectaminetrade mark 2000 Reagent (Invitrogen) in 0.2 ml of Opti-MEM(R) I (Invitrogen) according to the manufacturer's instructions. After the addition of the DNA-Lipofectaminetrade mark 2000-complexes to the dishes, the cells were incubated for a further 24 h at 37 degreesC and 10% CO2 without changing the medium.
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 0 62 0 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Analysis of Inositol Phosphate Formation in Intact COS-7 Cells</italic>
###xml 305 308 304 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">myo</italic>
###xml 312 313 311 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sup>
###xml 372 373 371 372 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 525 526 524 525 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 549 551 548 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref35">35</xref>
###xml 618 619 617 618 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 622 623 621 622 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 709 710 708 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</italic>
###xml 909 910 906 907 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 926 928 923 925 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>
###xml 974 975 971 972 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1016 1017 1013 1014 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1040 1041 1037 1038 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1113 1114 1110 1111 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1141 1142 1138 1139 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1399 1401 1387 1389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>
###xml 247 251 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">calf</span>
Analysis of Inositol Phosphate Formation in Intact COS-7 Cells-Twenty-four hours after transfection, the cells were washed once with 0.5 ml/well of buffer A and then supplied with 0.4 ml/well of Dulbecco's modified Eagle's medium containing fetal calf serum and supplements as specified above, 10 muCi/ml myo-[2-3H]inositol (catalog number TRK911; GE Healthcare), and 10 mm LiCl. The cells were incubated in this medium for 20 h, washed once with 0.4 ml/well of buffer A, and then lysed by the addition of 0.2 ml/well of 10 mm ice-cold formic acid (35). After keeping the samples on ice for 30 min, 0.3 ml/well of 10 mm NH4OH was added for neutralization, and the sample was centrifuged for 5 min at 15,000 x g. The supernatant was loaded onto a column containing 0.25 ml of Dowex(R) 1x8-200 ion exchange resin (catalog number 217425; Sigma) that had been converted to the formate form and equilibrated with H2O as described (34). The columns were washed once with 3 ml of H2O and then twice with 3.5 ml each of 60 mm sodium formate and 5 mm sodium tetraborate, and inositol phosphates were eluted with 3 ml of 1 m ammonium formate and 100 mm formic acid. The eluate was supplemented with 15 ml of scintillation fluid (Ultima Goldtrade mark; PerkinElmer Life Sciences), and the radioactivity was quantified by liquid scintillation counting. The columns were reused after regeneration, as described (34).
###end p 25

FIGURE 1.PLCgamma2 is activated by Rac2.A, domain organization of PLCgamma isoforms and their chimera. The common core domains (N-PH, EF, catalytic, and C2) and unique regions are shown. The PLCgammaW-XYZ nomenclature, used throughout, refers to W (PLCgamma isoform backbone), amino-terminal PH domain (X), N-terminal portion of spPH (Y), and C-terminal portion of spPH (Z). ###begin p 27
###xml 0 3 0 3 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">PLC</bold>
###xml 8 9 4 5 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 8 31 4 27 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><sub>2</sub> is activated by Rac2.</bold>
###xml 31 32 27 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 457 458 433 434 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 506 507 478 479 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 553 554 521 522 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 600 601 564 565 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 603 604 567 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 641 642 601 602 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 720 721 676 677 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 818 819 773 774 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 833 834 787 788 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 924 928 874 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">left</italic>
###xml 1028 1033 978 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
PLCgamma2 is activated by Rac2.A, domain organization of PLCgamma isoforms and their chimera. The common core domains (N-PH, EF, catalytic, and C2) and unique regions are shown. The PLCgammaW-XYZ nomenclature, used throughout, refers to W (PLCgamma isoform backbone), amino-terminal PH domain (X), N-terminal portion of spPH (Y), and C-terminal portion of spPH (Z). According to this designation, for example, construct PLCgamma1-122 corresponds to PLCgamma1 with the amino-terminal PH domain from PLCgamma1, the N-terminal portion of spPH from PLCgamma2, and C-terminal portion of spPH from PLCgamma2. B, the activation of purified PLCgamma2 by purified Rac2 can be reconstituted in vitro. Recombinant Rac2 and PLCgamma2 were purified from baculovirus-infected insect cells and reconstituted in the presence of 100 mum GDP or 100 mum GTPgammaS with phospholipid vesicles containing phosphatidylinositol (4,5)-bisphosphate (left). The purity of the preparations is also shown (analysis by SDS-PAGE and Coomassie Blue staining) (right).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NMR Spectroscopy</italic>
###xml 267 268 267 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">z</italic>
###xml 412 413 412 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 415 417 415 417 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 425 426 425 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 428 430 428 430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 480 481 480 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 483 485 483 485 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 569 571 569 571 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 578 580 578 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 692 694 692 694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref36">36</xref>
###xml 747 749 747 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref37">37</xref>
###xml 752 753 752 753 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 756 758 756 758 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 765 767 765 767 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 904 905 904 905 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 916 918 916 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref38">38</xref>
NMR Spectroscopy-NMR spectra were acquired at 298 K on a Varian UnityPLUS (500 MHz), Varian Inova (600 and 800 MHz), or Bruker Avance III spectrometer (700 MHz) equipped with either a triple resonance probe or a cryogenically cooled triple resonance probe, including z axis pulse field gradient coil. Sequence-specific resonance assignments were obtained using standard triple resonance NMR spectroscopy, namely 1H-15N HSQC, 1H-13C HSQC, HNCA, HN(CO)CA, HNCO, HNCACB, CBCA(CO)NH, 1H-15N TOCSY-HSQC, HC(C)H-TOCSY. Distance restraints were derived from three-dimensional 15N- and 13C-edited NOESY-HSQC spectra with a mixing time of 100 ms. All NMR spectra were processed using NMRPipe/NMRDraw (36) and analyzed using ANSIG for OpenGL version 1.0.3 (37). 1H, 13C, and 15N chemical shifts were referenced indirectly to sodium 2,2-dimethyl-2-silanepentane-5-sulfonate, using absolute frequency ratios for the 1H signals (38).
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 31 32 27 28 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 61 65 57 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G12V</sup>
###xml 172 174 168 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref39">39</xref>
###xml 379 380 371 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 395 396 387 388 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
The interaction of the PLCgamma2 spPH with GppNHp-loaded Rac2G12V (aa 2-177) was performed at constant concentration of spPH protein using the method previously described (39), ranging from spPH/Rac2 molar ratios of 1:0 to 1:1.1. Protein concentrations were estimated by using predicted extinction coefficients based upon amino acid composition. The concentration of the PLCgamma2 spPH was 0.5 mm. Any changes in the spectrum of labeled component during the titration can be attributed directly to an intermolecular interaction, since in each experiment both proteins are pre-exchanged into the same buffer.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Structure Calculations</italic>
###xml 121 123 121 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 140 142 140 142 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 179 180 175 176 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 563 565 559 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref40">40</xref>
Structure Calculations-Interproton distance restraints were derived from the ANSIG cross-peaks file of three-dimensional 15N NOESY-HSQC and 13C NOESY-HSQC spectra for the PLCgamma2 spPH domain. A proportion of the resonances were successfully assigned in a manual fashion without ambiguity. The remaining cross-peaks appearing at positions in the spectrum with overlapping resonances were labeled with ambiguous assignments by reference to the chemical shift list obtained with through-bond correlation spectra, using the "Connect" module from the program AZARA (40). The cross-peaks were grouped into five categories according to their relative peak intensities (strong, medium, weak, very weak, and very, very weak) and were designated with the corresponding interproton distance restraint limit of 1.8-2.5, 1.8-3.0, 1.8-3.5, 1.8-4.0, and 1.8-5.0 A, respectively. A distance of 0.5 A per methyl group was added to the upper bound of the distance restraint for NOE cross-peaks that involved methyl groups.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 49 58 49 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ab initio</italic>
###xml 112 114 112 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref41">41</xref>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref42">42</xref>
All structures for spPH were calculated using an ab initio simulated annealing protocol within the CNS program (41), with PARALLHDG version 5.3 force field and PROLSQ nonbonded energy function (42). The protocol adopts a mixture of Cartesian molecular dynamics and torsion angle dynamics simulated annealing to refine structures starting from random generated conformers with good local geometry.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 142 149 142 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 232 233 228 229 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 241 243 233 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 251 253 239 241 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 260 262 245 247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 270 272 255 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 338 340 323 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref43">43</xref>
A total of 2487 NOE-derived interproton distance restraints for spPH were included in the final iterations of the structure calculations (see Table 1). Backbone torsion angle restraints for phi and psi were derived from analysis of 1Halpha, 13Calpha, 13Cbeta, 13C', and 15NH chemical shift data bases as implemented in the program TALOS (43). Hydrogen bond restraints for amide protons were derived from an assessment of the regular secondary structure elements. This analysis included the overall and local patterns of NOEs and the pattern of amide proton solvent exchange rates. A total of 114 dihedral angle and 70 hydrogen bond (35 hydrogen bonds; two distance restraints per hydrogen bond) interatomic distance restraints were used for spPH.
###end p 32

###xml 1167 1169 1137 1139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 1171 1172 1141 1142 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</sub>
###xml 1170 1172 1140 1142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k<sub>a</sub></italic>
Biosensor Measurements-The biosensor measurements were carried out on the BIAcore 3000 system (GE Healthcare) at 25 degreesC. The sensor chip NTA was utilized and loaded with Ni2+ according to the manufacturer's instructions. Purified, hexahistidine-tagged Rac2G12V (aa 2-177) was loaded with GTPgammaS or GDPbetaS and immobilized in biosensor buffer (10 mm HEPES/NaOH, pH 8.0, 150 mm NaCl, 1 mm MgCl2, 5% (w/v) CM-dextran, and 0.01% (v/v) Nonidet P-40) at a flow rate of 5 mul/min for 5 min, which resulted in a deposition of approximately300 response units. Next, the purified analytes (full-length PLCgamma molecules or their isolated spPHs) were injected at varying concentrations. The values for nonspecific binding measured in the reference cell were subtracted. The evaluation of kinetic parameters was performed by nonlinear fitting of binding data using BiaEvaluation 2.1 software. The apparent association (ka) and dissociation rate (kd) constants were evaluated from the differential binding curves (Fc2 - Fc1) assuming an A + B = AB association type for the protein-protein interaction. The dissociation constant KD was calculated from the equation, KD = kd/ka.
###end p 38

Miscellaneous Methods-Recombinant baculoviruses were produced as described (44). ###begin title 42
RESULTS AND DISCUSSION
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">The PLC</italic>
###xml 12 13 8 9 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 13 80 9 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Split PH Domain Is Required for Isoform-specific Regulation by Rac2</italic>
###xml 176 177 168 169 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 208 210 196 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 297 298 281 282 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 471 472 451 452 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 545 546 525 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 539 546 519 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 589 590 565 566 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 689 690 657 658 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 808 809 772 773 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 932 933 892 893 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 968 969 924 925 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1076 1077 1031 1032 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1080 1082 1035 1037 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1117 1118 1072 1073 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1111 1118 1066 1073 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 1120 1124 1075 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">left</italic>
###xml 1239 1240 1190 1191 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1284 1285 1231 1232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1317 1318 1260 1261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1311 1318 1254 1261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 1320 1325 1263 1268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
###xml 1367 1368 1306 1307 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1403 1404 1338 1339 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1519 1527 1450 1458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1711 1712 1638 1639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1705 1712 1632 1639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 1737 1741 1664 1668 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G12V</sup>
###xml 1760 1761 1683 1684 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1778 1779 1697 1698 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1938 1939 1854 1855 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1998 1999 1910 1911 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 2099 2103 2004 2008 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G12V</sup>
###xml 2111 2112 2016 2017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 2105 2112 2010 2017 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 2176 2177 2078 2079 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 2215 2216 2113 2114 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 2413 2415 2311 2313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref45">45</xref>
The PLCgamma2Split PH Domain Is Required for Isoform-specific Regulation by Rac2-It has previously been shown with reconstitution experiments that Rac GTPases activate PLCgamma2 in the presence of GTPgammaS (12). These experiments were conducted with cell extracts enriched in recombinant PLCgamma2 and Rac2 that had been separately expressed in baculovirus-infected Sf9 cells. To exclude the possibility that other signaling proteins could mediate activation of PLCgamma2 by Rac, we set out to extend these data with purified components (Fig. 1B). We noted a 7-fold activation of PLCgamma2 by GTPgammaS-loaded Rac2. This result strongly suggests that Rac2 interacts directly with PLCgamma2 and that the presence of Rac2 is both necessary and sufficient for guanine nucleoside triphosphate-dependent PLCgamma2 activation. Next, we prepared a number of chimeric proteins where the N-terminal PH domains of the Rac-responsive PLCgamma2 and the Rac-nonresponsive PLCgamma1 were exchanged. The specific PLC activities of each of these chimeras were tested in the presence of 10 mum Ca2+ and shown to be comparable (Fig. 2A, left). However, when introduced into the reconstitution assay, it was evident that the N-terminal PH domain of PLCgamma2 does not impart Rac2 activation on PLCgamma1 (variant PLCgamma1-211) (Fig. 2A, right). Similarly, the exchange of the PLCgamma1 N-terminal PH domain into PLCgamma2 (variant PLCgamma2-122) did not significantly alter the propensity of this chimera to be activated by Rac2. These in vitro observations were further supported by experiments in intact COS-7 cells co-transfected with cDNAs encoding Rac2 and PLCgamma isozymes to display the same basal PLC activities (Fig. 3A). We confirmed that Rac2G12V activates PLCgamma2 but not PLCgamma1 and that the N-terminal PH domain is not involved in the Rac2-mediated activation. In addition, we showed that the Rac-binding N-terminal PH domain of PLCbeta2 is functionally interchangeable by constructing a PLCgamma1 chimera that incorporates this domain (variant PLCgamma1-beta11) and showing its activation by Rac2G12V (Fig. 3A). Together, these experiments suggest that, unlike with PLCbeta2, the N-terminal PH domain of PLCgamma2 is not involved in the observed interaction of Rac2. Furthermore, the findings support the idea that Rho family GTPase effector interaction sites are not conserved and cannot easily be predicted (45).
###end p 43

###begin p 46
###xml 290 291 282 283 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 366 367 358 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 608 610 596 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref46">46</xref>
###xml 612 614 600 602 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref47">47</xref>
###xml 743 744 721 722 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 754 755 732 733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 800 801 774 775 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 860 861 830 831 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 948 949 918 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 942 949 912 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 964 965 930 931 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1007 1008 969 970 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1016 1017 978 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1010 1017 972 979 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1019 1024 981 986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
###xml 1095 1096 1053 1054 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1116 1117 1070 1071 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1253 1254 1203 1204 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1304 1305 1250 1251 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1394 1395 1340 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 1388 1395 1334 1341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 1397 1402 1343 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
###xml 1562 1563 1504 1505 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1753 1754 1687 1688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1747 1754 1681 1688 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1801 1802 1731 1732 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1828 1829 1754 1755 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1993 1994 1915 1916 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 2025 2026 1943 1944 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 2112 2113 2026 2027 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
The PLCgamma isoforms contain a second PH domain within the specific array (SA) region located between the X and Y domains of the catalytic barrel. This spPH consists of two parts separated by the tandem array insert of two SH2 domains and an SH3 domain. Although the two halves of PLCgamma1 spPH can form a contiguous fold when expressed without the other domains (4), it is not known whether, in the context of the full-length PLCgamma molecules, these two sections also form a contiguous PH domain or are spatially separated. Recently, there have been reports that attribute different functions to spPHs (46, 47) with the insertion of other domains between either beta-strands 6 and 7 or beta-strands 3 and 4, as in the case of the PLCgamma1 isoform (4). Accordingly, we prepared chimeric PLCgamma1 proteins that contained either one or both of the PLCgamma2 spPH sections. The swapping of either the N- or C-terminal spPH subdomains (see Fig. 1A) from PLCgamma2 did not confer Rac activation on PLCgamma1 (Fig. 2B, right). However, the insertion of both partial spPH subdomains from PLCgamma2 produced a PLCgamma1 chimera that was stimulated 5.4-fold in activity by recombinant Rac2. The reverse chimera experiment was also carried out. The PLCgamma1 spPH subdomains were engineered into the PLCgamma2 polypeptide chain both as individual partial domains and as both halves together (Fig. 2C, right). The exchange of either or both of the partial domains abolished activation by Rac2 in reconstitution experiments. Therefore, both spPH subdomains of PLCgamma2 are necessary and sufficient to impart Rac2-dependent PLCgamma activation. This conclusion is supported by experiments that tested these PLCgamma chimeras in transfected COS-7 cells (Fig. 3B). Of note, the two spPH subdomains of PLCgamma2 also imparted on PLCgamma1 a marked sensitivity to activation by exogenous Vav1 and endogenous Rac GTPases present in COS-7 cells, whereas the presence of the two spPH subdomains of PLCgamma1 within the context of PLCgamma2 rendered the chimeric enzyme indistinguishable in this regard from wild-type PLCgamma1 (Fig. S1).
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 63 64 59 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 69 70 65 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 60 70 56 66 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">2, <italic>B</italic> and <italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 77 78 73 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 76 78 72 74 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 340 346 336 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7</xref>
###xml 481 482 473 474 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 648 649 640 641 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
The data obtained from the analysis of PLCgamma spPH (Figs. 2, B and C, and 3B), suggest that either the site of Rac2 interaction is distributed over both halves of spPH or that correct folding of each half requires the presence of the other from the same isoform. Since our further studies suggest that the first scenario is unlikely (see Fig. 7), the incorrect folding of each spPH half could be the reason for the loss of interaction with Rac. Indeed, recent studies of PLCgamma1 have shown that the construct of the isolated second half of its spPH was unfolded but that the interaction with the complementary half induces the correct folding (4). Since the sequence identity (29%) of the spPH regions of the PLCgamma isoforms is low, it is likely that their subdomains cannot be interchanged without losing correct spPH folding.
###end p 47
###begin p 48

###begin p 50
###xml 0 37 0 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">The Isolated Split PH Domain from PLC</italic>
###xml 42 43 38 39 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 42 62 38 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><sub>2</sub> Directly Binds Rac</italic>
###xml 95 96 87 88 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 166 167 154 155 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 180 181 164 165 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 280 288 264 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vitro</italic>
###xml 366 373 350 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 462 463 442 443 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 479 480 459 460 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 482 483 462 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 485 486 465 466 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">3</xref>
###xml 497 498 473 474 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 516 517 488 489 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 563 570 531 538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 598 599 562 563 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 649 650 609 610 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 759 760 707 708 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 781 782 725 726 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sub>
###xml 780 782 724 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>D</sub></italic>
###xml 799 800 742 743 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 887 888 827 828 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 891 892 831 832 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sub>
###xml 890 892 830 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>D</sub></italic>
###xml 909 910 848 849 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 927 929 866 868 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref26">26</xref>
###xml 959 960 894 895 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
The Isolated Split PH Domain from PLCgamma2 Directly Binds Rac-To evaluate the role of PLCgamma2 spPH as the site of Rac interaction, we purified a number of PLCgamma2 and PLCgamma1 variants (including the full-length and isolated spPHs) in order to carry out interaction studies in vitro. For comprehensive, quantitative analysis we used surface plasmon resonance (Table 1). Consistent with the data where we analyzed the requirements for activation of PLCgamma2 by Rac2 (Figs. 1, 2, 3), PLCgamma2, but not PLCgamma1, selectively bound GTPgammaS-activated Rac2 (Table 1). Furthermore, the PLCgamma1 chimera incorporating both halves of the PLCgamma2 spPH (PLCgamma1-122) was fully functional in Rac2-GTPgammaS binding. The strength of the binding of PLCgamma2 and PLCgamma1-122 (KD = 3.9 and 5.8 mum, respectively) was similar to that determined in this and a previous study for PLCbeta2 (KD = 6.0 and 7.0 mum, respectively) (26). These data confirm PLCgamma2 as a direct effector of Rac and show that its spPH determines the isoform specificity for this interaction.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 33 34 29 30 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 147 148 135 136 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 155 156 143 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 192 193 176 177 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 472 473 452 453 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 509 510 485 486 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 523 524 495 496 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 573 574 541 542 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 675 676 635 636 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 727 734 687 694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 770 771 726 727 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 789 790 745 746 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sub>
###xml 788 790 744 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>D</sub></italic>
###xml 798 799 753 754 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 904 905 856 857 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 907 909 859 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref26">26</xref>
###xml 969 970 918 919 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1022 1024 971 973 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
We also assessed whether PLCgamma2 spPH in isolation can bind GTPgammaS-activated Rac2. Based on the recent structural characterization of PLCgamma1 spPH (4), we designed a contiguous PLCgamma2 spPH construct lacking the intervening SH2 and SH3 domains and being replaced by a linker consisting of the remaining natural loop regions. In essence, a "regular" PH domain is predicted to be formed by the directly linked spPH subdomains. The corresponding domain from PLCgamma1 was also constructed. Both PLCgamma2 and PLCgamma1 spPHs could be prepared in good yields. PLCgamma2 spPH selectively bound Rac2-GTPgammaS, similar to the full-length protein; importantly, for PLCgamma1 spPH, no interaction with Rac2 could be detected (Table 1). The binding strength for PLCgamma2 spPH with Rac2 (KD = 17 mum) is in close agreement with previously reported affinities of Rac2 for the isolated PH domain of PLCbeta2 (26). Subsequent structural studies have shown that the PLCbeta2 isoform contacts Rac solely through its PH domain (23).
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 45 46 41 42 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 68 75 64 71 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 107 108 103 104 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sub>
###xml 106 108 102 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>D</sub></italic>
###xml 167 168 160 161 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 174 176 167 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref26">26</xref>
###xml 198 200 185 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref22">22</xref>
###xml 288 290 275 277 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref48">48</xref>
###xml 301 309 288 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vitro</italic>
###xml 433 435 420 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref49">49</xref>
###xml 437 439 424 426 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref50">50</xref>
###xml 645 646 628 629 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 698 699 677 678 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 710 711 685 686 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 776 777 751 752 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 803 805 778 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref51">51</xref>
###xml 1163 1164 1126 1127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1157 1164 1120 1127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1166 1170 1129 1133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">left</italic>
###xml 1227 1228 1190 1191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1221 1228 1184 1191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1230 1235 1193 1198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
The strengths of interaction between PLCgamma2 and Rac2 shown here (Table 1), in the micromolar range for KD, are generally consistent with values obtained for PLCbeta2-Rac (26) and PLCepsilon-Ras (22) complexes and more broadly with a number of other small GTPase-effector interactions (48) measured in vitro. There are, however, instances of Rac- and Cdc42-effector interactions with dissociation constants in the nanomolar range (49, 50). However, in a cellular setting, the posttranslationally modified C terminus of Rac2 or the plasma membrane could be involved in stabilizing the interaction between activated Rac2 and full-length PLCgamma2. It is important to note that the spPHs of PLCgamma1 and -gamma2 are unlikely to bind to membrane lipids directly. Experimental (4) and molecular modeling (51) studies agree that these domains do not possess the amino acid sequence motifs typical of lipid binding modules. Accordingly, although some changes in the subcellular distribution do occur with some of the chimeras (PLCgamma1-121, PLCgamma1-112, and PLCgamma2-221) (Fig. S2), these effects do not correlate with the variation in activity observed in Fig. 3B (left), which are also evident in the cell-free system (Fig. 2B, right).
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 0 30 0 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Structural Analysis of the PLC</italic>
###xml 35 36 31 32 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 36 83 32 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Split PH Domain Interaction Interface with Rac2</italic>
###xml 163 164 155 156 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 290 292 282 284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 307 309 299 301 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 311 313 303 305 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 351 352 339 340 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 484 485 472 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 478 485 466 473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 538 540 526 528 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">15</sup>
###xml 547 549 535 537 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">13</sup>
###xml 558 559 546 547 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 736 743 724 731 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1017 1018 1005 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1011 1018 999 1006 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1062 1083 1050 1071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ribbon representation</italic>
###xml 1093 1094 1081 1082 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 1087 1094 1075 1082 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 1252 1253 1233 1234 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1841 1842 1780 1781 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
Structural Analysis of the PLCgamma2Split PH Domain Interaction Interface with Rac2-To provide a basis for further analysis of the interaction between the PLCgamma2 spPH and Rac2, we determined the three-dimensional solution structure of the spPH by heteronuclear NMR spectroscopy. Single (15N) and double (13C,15N) isotope-labeled samples of PLCgamma2 spPH were prepared, and nearly complete resonance assignments were obtained using standard triple resonance NMR experiments (Fig. 4A). On the basis of the analysis of three-dimensional 15N- and 13C-edited 1H NOESY spectra, 2487 interproton distance restraints were obtained and used in structure calculations along with 70 hydrogen bond restraints and 114 dihedral angle restraints. Table 2 shows the structural statistics for the bundle of 20 lowest energy conformers, each of which displays low restraint violations and good stereochemical and nonbonded interaction scores. The best fit superposition of the backbone atoms of the conformer set is shown in Fig. 4B. The lowest energy structure is shown in a ribbon representation in Fig. 4C, demonstrating the conserved core structure of a partially open two-sheet beta-barrel with one end capped by the C-terminal helix. As predicted, the PLCgamma2 spPH structure conforms well with the canonical PH domain architecture with seven beta-strands and one alpha-helix: residues 478-485 (beta1); 490-499 (beta2) and 502-506 (beta3) from the N-terminal spPH subdomain; 851-853 (beta4); 860-863 (beta5); 873-876 (beta6); 886-889 (beta7); and 893-906 (alpha1) from the C-terminal spPH subdomain. Omitting the loop between beta3 and beta4, which contains the linker between the spPH subdomains, and a small number of apparently flexible residues at the N and C termini, the refined conformer bundle provides a well defined model for the PLCgamma2 spPH with coordinate root mean square difference values of 0.41 +/- 0.05 A for the backbone and 0.76 +/- 0.06 A for all heavy atoms (residues 478-508 and 849-908).
###end p 53

###xml 1693 1694 1643 1644 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</sup>
###xml 1814 1816 1764 1766 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1818 1820 1768 1770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 1849 1851 1799 1801 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1853 1855 1803 1805 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 1886 1888 1836 1838 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1892 1894 1842 1844 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 1340 1895 1290 1845 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="57">Sum averaging of NOE distance restraints was used for groups with degenerate proton chemical shifts. The interproton unambiguous distance restraint list comprised 786 intraresidue, 553 sequential (|<italic>i - j</italic>| = 1|), 373 short range (1 &lt; |<italic>i - j</italic>| &lt; 5), and 776 long range (|<italic>i - j</italic>| &gt; 5). Hydrogen bond restraints were applied as pairs of distance restraints: H<sup>N</sup>&#183;&#183;&#183;O, 1.2-2.2 &#197;; N&#183;&#183;&#183;O, 1.2-3.2 &#197;. The final values for the respective force constants were as follows: NOE, 30 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> &#197;<sup>&#8722;2</sup>; hydrogen bonds, 50 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> &#197;<sup>&#8722;2</sup>; dihedral angles, 200 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> rad<sup>&#8722;2</sup>.</p>
###xml 1339 1895 1289 1845 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="tblfn3"><label>a</label><p textid="57">Sum averaging of NOE distance restraints was used for groups with degenerate proton chemical shifts. The interproton unambiguous distance restraint list comprised 786 intraresidue, 553 sequential (|<italic>i - j</italic>| = 1|), 373 short range (1 &lt; |<italic>i - j</italic>| &lt; 5), and 776 long range (|<italic>i - j</italic>| &gt; 5). Hydrogen bond restraints were applied as pairs of distance restraints: H<sup>N</sup>&#183;&#183;&#183;O, 1.2-2.2 &#197;; N&#183;&#183;&#183;O, 1.2-3.2 &#197;. The final values for the respective force constants were as follows: NOE, 30 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> &#197;<sup>&#8722;2</sup>; hydrogen bonds, 50 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> &#197;<sup>&#8722;2</sup>; dihedral angles, 200 kcal mol<sup>&#8722;1</sup> rad<sup>&#8722;2</sup>.</p></fn>
